## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time and population size, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. The relationship likely involves density-dependent feedback through P and possibly time-varying environmental conditions through t.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth, slower near capacity)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Logistic with harvest: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal environmental variation)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism balance)
- Exponential decay toward capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (exponentially modified density dependence)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying intrinsic growth rate)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Population growth rate proportional to P indicates density-independent (Malthusian) component → multiplicative c*P term
- Negative quadratic term in P (like -c*P²) indicates intraspecific competition / carrying capacity limitation
- Cubic terms in P (positive-negative-positive pattern) suggest Allee effects with both lower and upper population bounds
- Logarithmic dependence on P (e.g., log(c/P)) indicates Gompertz-type asymmetric approach to carrying capacity
- Ratio forms P/(1+c*P) indicate contest competition where resources are divided among individuals
- Periodic functions of time (sin, cos of t) indicate seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing
- dP/dt passing through zero at specific P values identifies equilibrium points (carrying capacity, extinction threshold)
- If dP/dt depends only on P and not t, the system is autonomous — time-invariance suggests stable environmental conditions
- Fractional powers of P (P^c where 0<c<1) suggest surface-area-to-volume scaling in metabolic growth models
- Exponential dependence on t in the growth rate coefficient suggests progressive environmental degradation or improvement
